HiC-Pro: an optimized and flexible pipeline for Hi-C data processing. Genome Biol. 16, 259 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1867">79</a></sup> to remove duplicates and then assessed quality. After trimming low-quality reads and removing adapters, more than 22.31 Gb (~112.89-fold coverage) of clean data was generated. Then, all clean data were submitted to the 3D-DNA v180419 pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Dudchenko, O. et al. De novo assembly of the Aedes aegypti genome using Hi-C yields chromosome-length scaffolds. Science 356, 92–95 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1871">80</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Genome assembly</h3><p>Approximately 79.49 Gb of raw reads was generated by sequencing all six DNA libraries. These raw reads were filtered following a previous study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Wu, H. et al. A high-quality Actinidia chinensis (kiwifruit) genome. Hortic. Res. 6, 1–9 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1883">81</a></sup>. We first used Trimmomatic v0.33<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Bolger, A. M., Lohse, M. &amp; Usadel, B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics 30, 2114–2120 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1887">82</a></sup> to perform quality filtering of short reads. We then used the BFC error corrector<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Li, H. BFC: correcting Illumina sequencing errors. Bioinformatics 31, 2885–2887 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1891">83</a></sup> followed by FastUniq v1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Xu, H. et al. FastUniq: a fast de novo duplicates removal tool for paired short reads. PLoS ONE 7, e52249 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1895">84</a></sup> to delete duplicates in the mate pair data. The resultant reads produced approximately 59.77 Gb of clean data (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#MOESM2">1</a>).</p><p>We used Platanus v1.2.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Kajitani, R. et al. Efficient de novo assembly of highly heterozygous genomes from whole-genome shotgun short reads. Genome Res. 24, 1384–1395 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1905">85</a></sup> software to perform <i>de novo</i> assembly of the <i>L. maritima</i> genome. Thereafter, using the 3D-DNA v180419 pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Dudchenko, O. et al. De novo assembly of the Aedes aegypti genome using Hi-C yields chromosome-length scaffolds. Science 356, 92–95 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1915">80</a></sup>, the draft assembly was scaffolded with the Hi–C clean reads. Using the Juicer v1.6.2 pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicer provides a one-click system for analyzing loop-resolution Hi-C experiments. Cell Syst. 3, 95–98 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1919">86</a></sup>, we aligned the Hi–C clean reads to the draft assembly genome. We then used Juicebox Assembly Tools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicebox provides a visualization system for Hi-C contact maps with unlimited zoom. Cell Systems 3, 99–101, &#xA;                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cels.2015.07.012&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1924">87</a></sup> to polish the results from the 3D-DNA v180419 pipeline. The Hi–C scaffolding was anchored on 12 pseudochromosomes. In total, 88.31% of the assembled sequences were related to the pseudochromosomes. In addition, we assessed the quality of the assembled genome using the BUSCO v4.1.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Simão, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210–3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1928">35</a></sup> pipeline (database: embryophyta odb10, 2020-09-02, containing 1,614 BUSCO genes).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Repeat element annotation</h3><p>Repeat elements were identified with the RepeatMasker v4.0.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Tarailo-Graovac, M. &amp; Chen, N. Using RepeatMasker to identify repetitive elements in genomic sequences. In Current Protocols in Bioinformatics (John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc., 2002)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1940">88</a></sup> and RepeatModeler v1.0.11<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Jurka, J. et al. Repbase Update, a database of eukaryotic repetitive elements. Cytogenet. Genome Res. 110, 462–467 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1944">89</a></sup> programs using the assembled <i>L. maritima</i> genome as the input. We also identified intact LTR retrotransposons by searching the <i>L. maritima</i> genome using LTRharvest v1.5.10<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Ellinghaus, D., Kurtz, S. &amp; Willhoeft, U. LTRharvest, an efficient and flexible software for de novo detection of LTR retrotransposons. BMC Bioinform. 9, 18 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1954">90</a></sup> and LTR_Finder v1.06<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W265–W268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1959">91</a></sup>. We further combined these results using LTR_retriever v1.9<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Ou, S. &amp; Jiang, N. LTR_retriever: a highly accurate and sensitive program for identification of long terminal repeat retrotransposons. Plant Physiol. 176, 1410–1422 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1963">92</a></sup>. We also estimated insertion time according to a substitution rate of 7 × 10<sup>−9</sup>/site/year.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Gene prediction and annotation</h3><p>To predict genes in the <i>L. maritima</i> genome, we first assembled transcripts using the <i>de novo</i> and genome-guided modes in Trinity v2.6.6<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Haas, B. J. et al. De novo transcript sequence reconstruction from RNA-seq using the Trinity platform for reference generation and analysis. Nat. Protoc. 8, 1494–1512 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1984">93</a></sup>. Then, these transcripts were used to create transcript-based predictions with the PASA v2.1.0 pipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 5654–5666 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d51408e1988">94</a></sup>. We also carried out homolog predictions. In such predictions, the protein sequences of <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>A. arabicum</i>, <i>A. lyrata</i>, <i>Eutrema yunnanense</i>, <i>Brassica rapa</i>, <i>Sisymbrium irio</i>, <i>C. rubella</i>, <i>Tarenaya hassleriana</i>, <i>Leavenworthia alabamica</i> and <i>Carica papaya</i> were mapped to the <i>L. maritima</i> genome using Exonerate v2.2.0 (<a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate</a>). GlimmerHMM v3.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2034">95</a></sup> and Augustus v3.2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Stanke, M., Steinkamp, R., Waack, S. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene finding in eukaryotes. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, W309–W312 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2039">96</a></sup> were trained with genes from the PASA results and used for <i>de novo</i> gene prediction. We merged the gene models from the three sources using EVidenceModeler v1.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, 1–22 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2046">97</a></sup>. To annotate the functions of all predicted genes, we aligned the protein sequences of <i>L. maritima</i> to Swiss-Prot and TrEMBL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Bairoch, A. &amp; Apweiler, R. The SWISS-PROT protein sequence database and its supplement TrEMBL in 2000. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 45–48 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2053">36</a></sup> using blastp and generated functional assignments based on the best hit. Protein domains were determined by searching against the InterPro<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Hunter, S. et al. InterPro: the integrative protein signature database. Nucleic Acids Res. 37, D211–D215 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2057">37</a></sup> database. In addition, Blast2GO v2.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Conesa, A. et al. Blast2GO: a universal tool for annotation, visualization and analysis in functional genomics research. Bioinformatics 21, 3674–3676 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2062">98</a></sup> was used to identify the Gene Ontology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Ashburner, M. et al. Gene ontology: tool for the unification of biology. Nat. Genet. 25, 25 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2066">38</a></sup> annotations and KEGG<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Kanehisa, M. &amp; Goto, S. KEGG: Kyoto encyclopedia of genes and genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 28, 27–30 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2070">39</a></sup> pathways using the KAAS server (<a href="https://www.genome.jp/kegg/kaas">https://www.genome.jp/kegg/kaas</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Synteny and WGD</h3><p>To construct syntenic blocks between <i>L. maritima</i> and <i>C. rubella</i>, all protein sequences of <i>L. maritima</i> were compared to protein sequences of <i>C. rubella</i>. The gene pairs with an <i>e</i>-value ≤ 1e-5 were further analyzed. We applied the ColinearScan v1.0.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Wang, X. et al. Statistical inference of chromosomal homology based on gene colinearity and applications to Arabidopsis and rice. BMC Bioinforma. 7, 447 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2105">41</a></sup> program, which can effectively evaluate genomic blocks of collinear genes, and the MCScanX v1 package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2109">42</a></sup> to find the syntenic blocks between the <i>C. rubella</i> and <i>L. maritima</i> genomes. Thereafter, we used these collinear gene pairs to construct a dotplot. Next, we used the script “add_ka_and_ks_to_collinearity.pl” in MCScanX to calculate the Ks values of the collinear orthologous gene pairs. We converted the Ks values to divergence times (T) based on <i>T</i> = <i>K</i>s/2<i>r</i>, where r is the neutral substitution rate (8.22 × 10<sup>−9</sup>). Finally, we performed evolutionary rate correction because of the inconsistent evolutionary rates among species. The evolutionary rate correction method was as reported by Wang et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Wang, J. et al. Two likely auto-tetraploidization events shaped kiwifruit genome and contributed to establishment of the Actinidiaceae family. iScience 7, 230–240 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2131">46</a></sup>. Briefly, under the assumption that the <i>C. rubella</i> peak appears at <i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub> and the <i>L. maritima</i> peak appears at <i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub>, we can use the equation <i>r</i> = (<i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> − <i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub>)/<i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub> to describe the relative evolutionary rate of <i>L. maritima</i>. Then, rate correction was performed to discover the corrected rate <i>k</i><sub><i>L</i> correction</sub> of <i>L. maritima</i> relative to <i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub>: (1) For the Ks between duplicates in <i>L. maritima</i>, we defined the correction coefficient <i>W</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> as <i>k</i><sub>L correction</sub>/<i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> = <i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub>/<i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> = <i>W</i><sub><i>L</i></sub>; thus, we obtained <i>k</i><sub>L correction</sub> = <i>k</i><sub><i>C</i></sub>/<i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> × <i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> = 1/(1 + r) × <i>k</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> and <i>W</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> = 1/(1 + r). (2) For the Ks between homologous genes from <i>C. rubella</i> and <i>L. maritima</i>, if the peak was located at <i>k</i><sub><i>L-C</i></sub>, supposing the correction coefficient <i>W</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> in <i>L. maritima</i>, we then calculated a corrected evolutionary rate <i>k</i><sub>L-C-correction</sub> = <i>W</i><sub><i>L</i></sub> × k<sub><i>L-C</i>.</sub></p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Phylogeny and divergence</h3><p>The genomes of <i>L. maritima</i> and 10 other species (<i>A. arabicum</i>, <i>B. rapa</i>, <i>L. alabamica</i>, <i>E. yunnanense</i>, <i>S. irio</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>A. lyrata</i>, <i>C. rubella</i>, <i>S. parvula</i> and <i>Thlaspi arvense</i>) were selected to generate clusters of gene families. We retained only the longest protein sequence. We removed redundant sequences based on alternative splicing variations. Using OrthoFinder v2.3.12<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Emms, D. M. &amp; Kelly, S. OrthoFinder: solving fundamental biases in whole genome comparisons dramatically improves orthogroup inference accuracy. Genome Biol. 16, 157 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2350">47</a></sup>, we obtained orthologous gene families. Protein sequences from 1986 single-copy gene families were used to construct a phylogenetic tree. MAFFT v7.313<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Standley, D. M. MAFFT multiple sequence alignment software version 7: improvements in performance and usability. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 772–780 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2354">99</a></sup> software was used for sequence alignment of each single-copy gene family with default settings. A phylogenetic tree was built using RAxML v8.0.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312–1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2358">100</a></sup> under the PROTGAMMALGX model, and divergence times were calculated using the MCMCTree program of the PAML v4.9 package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2362">54</a></sup>. The calibration information for MCMCTree was extracted based on the TimeTree database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Hedges, S. B., Dudley, J. &amp; Kumar, S. TimeTree: a public knowledge-base of divergence times among organisms. Bioinformatics 22, 2971–2972 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2366">101</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.time.org/">http://www.time.org/</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Gene family expansion and contraction</h3><p>Based on the dated phylogeny, we determined the expansions and contractions of orthologous gene families in the 11 Brassicaceae species (<i>A. arabicum</i>, <i>B. rapa</i>, <i>L. alabamica</i>, <i>E. yunnanense</i>, <i>S. irio</i>, <i>T. arvense, C. rubella</i>, <i>A. thaliana</i>, <i>A. lyrata</i>, <i>S. parvula</i>, and <i>L. maritima</i>) by using the CAFÉ v4.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="De Bie, T., Cristianini, N., Demuth, J. P. &amp; Hahn, M. W. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics 22, 1269–1271 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2416">102</a></sup> program. Genes in significantly expanded families were then used for Gene Ontology enrichment analysis.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Genes under positive selection</h3><p>We selected six genomes, i.e., those of <i>A. arabicum</i>, <i>A. lyrata</i>, <i>C. rubella</i>, <i>E. yunnanense</i>, <i>S. parvula</i> and <i>L. maritima</i>, to identify orthologs for analyzing positive selection. First, Proteinortho v6.0.21<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Lechner, M. et al. Proteinortho: detection of (co-)orthologs in large-scale analysis. BMC Bioinform. 12, 124 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2447">103</a></sup> was used to detect orthologs among the six genomes. Next, we used the PosiGene v0.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Sahm, A., Bens, M., Platzer, M. &amp; Szafranski, K. PosiGene: automated and easy-to-use pipeline for genome-wide detection of positively selected genes. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, e100 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00422-w#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d51408e2451">104</a></sup> pipeline for genome-wide detection of the genes with positive selection and specified the <i>L. maritima</i> clade as the foreground branch. Finally, PSGs were identified based on an FDR-corrected <i>P</i> value &lt; 0.05.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Raw Illumina-short reads and Hi–C reads used for de novo whole-genome assembly have been deposited in the National Center for Biotechnology Information (NCBI) Sequence Read Archive database under accession number PRJNA630530. The genome and related annotation data have been deposited in the National Genomics Data Center (PRJCA002888).</p>

                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="AH. Paterson, JE. Bowers, BA. Chapman, " /><meta itemprop="datePublished" content="2004" /><meta itemprop="headline" content="Paterson, A. H., Bowers, J. E. &amp; Chapman, B. A.
